1	"""Naive PyTorch reference for Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form.
2	
3	This is the correctness oracle, NOT the SOTA baseline. It mirrors the
4	chunk-parallel formulation in fla/ops/kda/naive.py (Songlin Yang et al.)
5	without any Triton or CUDA optimization.
6	
7	Inputs (per the FLA convention):
8	  q, k : (B, T, H, K)   bf16   -- queries / keys
9	  v    : (B, T, H, V)   bf16   -- values
10	  g    : (B, T, H, K)   fp32   -- per-channel log-decay (in-chunk cumsum applied)
11	  beta : (B, T, H)      bf16   -- write strength
12	
13	Output:
14	  o    : (B, T, H, V)   bf16
15	
16	The agent must reproduce this output (within bf16 tolerance) using a CUTLASS
17	CuTe kernel on SM120 -- NOT by calling fla.ops.chunk_kda directly.
18	"""
19	from __future__ import annotations
20	
21	import torch
22	import torch.nn as nn
23	from einops import rearrange
24	
25	OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
26	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
27	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
28	
29	
30	def _naive_chunk_kda(
31	    q: torch.Tensor,
32	    k: torch.Tensor,
33	    v: torch.Tensor,
34	    g: torch.Tensor,
35	    beta: torch.Tensor,
36	    scale: float,
37	    chunk_size: int = 64,
38	) -> torch.Tensor:
39	    """KDA forward, no initial state, no final state. Returns o with v's dtype."""
40	    dtype = v.dtype
41	    B, T, H, K = q.shape
42	    V = v.shape[-1]
43	    BT = chunk_size
44	    assert T % BT == 0, f"T={T} must be a multiple of chunk_size={BT}"
45	    NT = T // BT
46

1	"""Canonical shape sweep for KDA forward (chunk form).
2	
3	Mix of:
4	  - short-context training-step scale (T=1024)
5	  - mid-context (T=2048) which is the headline benchmark
6	  - long-context that stresses the inter-chunk recurrence (T=4096)
7	  - thin-batch decode-style (B=1, T=2048, fewer heads)
8	
9	Constraints:
10	  - T % chunk_size == 0 (chunk_size = 64)
11	  - K, V are the per-head channel dims; KDA in Kimi Linear uses K=V=128
12	"""

1	I need you to implement Kimi Delta Attention forward (chunk form) for the B200 (SM100 Blackwell, HBM3e, 8 TB/s). The reference implementation is in reference.py and your kernel goes in solution.py. You can make whatever mess you want in this directory — scratch files, intermediate kernels, build artifacts, profiling traces — but the final answer has to be in solution.py with the same Model, get_inputs, and get_init_inputs interface as reference.py.
2	
3	The op is the chunk-parallel KDA forward from the FLA library: q and k of shape (B, T, H, K) in bf16, v of shape (B, T, H, V) in bf16, g of shape (B, T, H, K) in fp32 (per-channel log-decay with in-chunk cumsum already applied), beta of shape (B, T, H) in bf16, scale a python float, chunk_size 64, no initial state, no final state. You return o of shape (B, T, H, V) in bf16. Correctness tolerance is 0.05 abs/rel — the long recurrence accumulates more error than a single GEMM so the bar's a bit looser than default bf16. The shapes you have to handle are B=2 T=1024 H=8 K=128 V=128 (short-context training step), B=2 T=2048 H=8 K=128 V=128 (the headline shape from the Kimi Linear paper), B=1 T=4096 H=8 K=128 V=128 (long context that stresses the inter-chunk recurrence), and B=1 T=2048 H=4 K=128 V=128 (thin batch decode).
4

1	name: 02_kda_cutlass
2	display_name: "Kimi Delta Attention (chunk forward) via CUTLASS CuTe"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: compute
5	
6	# Approximate FLOPs per forward call. KDA forward (chunk form) breakdown per
7	# token across all heads:
8	#   - intra-chunk Aqk (q @ k.T with decay): 2*BT*K
9	#   - intra-chunk Akk + cumulative invert : ~3*BT*K + BT^2
10	#   - w = A @ (g.exp()*k):                  2*BT*K
11	#   - u = A @ v:                            2*BT*V
12	#   - inter-chunk q @ S:                    2*K*V
13	#   - inter-chunk (Aqk @ v_i):              2*BT*V
14	#   - state update S += k.T @ v_i:          2*K*V
15	# Aggregating with a constant of 4 (typical for chunked linear attention) gives
16	# the formula below. Used only for roofline reporting -- not graded directly.
17	flops_formula: "4 * B * T * H * (K*V + CHUNK_SIZE*K + CHUNK_SIZE*V)"
18	
19	# Bytes moved (lower bound): one read of q,k,v,g,beta and one write of o.
20	bytes_formula: "B*T*H*K*2 + B*T*H*K*2 + B*T*H*V*2 + B*T*H*K*4 + B*T*H*2 + B*T*H*V*2"
21	
22	hardware: [B200]
23	peak_tflops_key: bf16  # KDA's heavy work is bf16 @ bf16 -> fp32 GEMM-equivalent
24	peak_bandwidth_key: dram
25	
26	# bf16 default tolerance from src/eval/correctness.py is 1e-2 atol/rtol; KDA's
27	# long recurrence accumulates more error than a single GEMM, so we relax slightly.
28	tolerance:
29	  torch.bfloat16: 0.05  # was "5e-2" -- PyYAML parses un-dotted sci-notation as string

stdout (1010 chars)
1	"""Roofline math: achieved TFLOPS / GB/s, peak fraction.
2	
3	FLOPS and bytes formulas come from the problem's `problem.yaml`. They are the
4	dense-equivalent algorithmic work; kernels that skip work (sparsity, early
5	exit) are still measured against the dense cost.
6	"""
7	from __future__ import annotations
8	
9	
10	def compute_tflops(flops: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
11	    """flops per invocation and wall time in ms -> TFLOPS."""
12	    if time_ms <= 0:
13	        return 0.0
14	    return flops / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e12
15	
16	
17	def compute_gbps(bytes_moved: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
18	    """bytes per invocation and wall time in ms -> GB/s."""
19	    if time_ms <= 0:
20	        return 0.0
21	    return bytes_moved / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e9
22	
23	
24	def peak_fraction(
25	    achieved: float,
26	    peak: float,
27	) -> float:
28	    """Return achieved / peak, clamped to [0, infinity)."""
29	    if peak <= 0:
30	        return 0.0
31	    return max(0.0, achieved / peak)
32

1	"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.
2	
3	All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
4	implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.
5	
6	Methodology:
7	  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
8	    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
9	  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
10	    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
11	    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
12	  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
13	    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
14	  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.
15	
16	Notes / known biases not addressed here:
17	  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
18	    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
19	    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
20	    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
21	    "compiled" baseline policy.
22	  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
23	  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
24	    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
25	    instrumentation if you ever care.
26	"""
27	from __future__ import annotations
28	
29	import os
30	import re
31

(M + I) then multiply by beta[...,None,:] which broadcasts over rows: result[i,c] = (M[i,c]+δ_{ic}) * beta[c]. So A_final = (M+I) · diag(β) where diag(β) scales columns. = (I-A0)^{-1} · diag(β). So **A_final = (I - A0)^{-1} · diag(β)**. where A0[i,c] = -β[i] * <k[c]⊙exp(g[c]-g[i]), k[i]> for c<i, else 0. (Strictly lower triangular.) Then: ```python w = A @ (g.exp() * k) # A_final @ (exp(g)*k). w has shape (b,h,n,BT,K). u = A @ v # (b,h,n,BT,V) ``` So: - w[i,d] = sum_c A_final[i,c] * exp(g[c,d]) * k[c,d] - u[i,:] = sum_c A_final[i,c] * v[c,:] **Inter-chunk recurrence:** ```python S = zeros(B,H,K,V) # (b,h,K,V) state, per (b,h) o = zeros_like(v) mask_strict_upper = triu(ones(BT,BT,bool), diagonal=1) for i in range(NT): q_i, k_i, u_i, g_i, w_i = q[:,:,i], k[:,:,i], u[:,:,i], g[:,:,i], w[:,:,i] # each (b,h,BT,d) Aqk = zeros(b,h,BT,BT) for j in range(BT): k_j = k[:,:,i,j] # (b,h,K) g_j = g[:,:,i,j:j+1,:] # (b,h,1,K) Aqk[...,j] = einsum("... c d, ... d -> ... c", q_i * (g_i - g_j).exp(), k_j) # Aqk[..., j, c] = sum_d q_i[c,d] * exp(g_i[c,d]-g_j[0,d]) * k_j[d] = q[c]·k[j]*exp(g[c]-g[j]) Aqk = Aqk.masked_fill(mask_strict_upper, 0) # keep c<=j (lower tri incl diagonal) # Aqk[j,c] for c<=j: sum_d q[c] exp(g[c]-g[j]) k[j] v_i = u_i - w_i @ S # w_i (b,h,BT,K) @ S (b,h,K,V) -> (b,h,BT,V). v_i[i_pos,:] = u_i[i_pos] - w_i[i_pos] @ S o[:,:,i] = (q_i * g_i.exp()) @ S + Aqk @ v_i # (q_i*exp(g_i)) @ S: (b,h,BT,K)@(b,h,K,V) -> (b,h,BT,V) S = S * rearrange(g_i[:,:,-1].exp(), "b h k -> b h k 1") # scale state by exp(g at last position of chunk) S = S + rearrange((g_i[:,:,-1:] - g_i).exp() * k_i, "b h c k -> b h k c") @ v_i # (g_i last - g_i).exp() * k_i: (b,h,BT,K). rearrange to (b,h,K,BT). @ v_i (b,h,BT,V) -> (b,h,K,V) ``` Let me get the indexing for Aqk right. import torch, triton
@triton.jit
def k(x_ptr, y_ptr, n):
    pid = triton.program_id(0)
    offs = pid*64 + triton.arange(0,64)
    m = tl.load(x_ptr+offs, mask=offs<n)
    tl.store(y_ptr+offs, m*2.0+1.0, mask=offs<n)
import triton.language as tl

import torch, triton, triton.language as tl
@triton.jit
def axpy(x_ptr, y_ptr, N, B: tl.constexpr):
    pid = tl.program_id(0)
    offs = pid*B + tl.arange(0,B)
    m = offs < N
    x = tl.load(x_ptr+offs, mask=m)
    tl.store(y_ptr+offs, x*3.0+1.0, mask=m)
x = torch.randn(1024, device='cuda'); y = torch.empty_like(x)
axpy[(16,)](x,y,1024,1024//16)
torch.cuda.synchronize()
print('triton ok', (y==x*3+1).all().item())
# check blackwell mma
print('triton arch', triton.runtime.driver.active.get_current_target())
EOF

This is very informative. The FLA KDA intra uses a sub-chunk decomposition with BC=16. The key insight: it splits the BT=64 chunk into NC=4 sub-chunks of BC=16. It computes diagonal blocks, does forward substitution, then merges off-diagonal blocks via matrix products. This is the efficient way to compute (I-A0)^{-1}. This is sophisticated. For my first implementation, I don't need to replicate this exact structure — I need correctness and then performance. The forward substitution (the sequential prefix within BC=16) is the core. Key takeaways for the math: - They use `exp2` (base-2 exp) with g scaled by RCP_LN2. But reference.py uses natural exp and no scale. I'll use natural exp to match reference.py. (exp2 vs exp: mathematically 2^x = e^(x ln2). FLA scales g by 1/ln2 so exp2(g/ln2) = e^g. Same result. I'll just use e^g directly / tl.exp.) - The forward substitution algorithm: For each sub-chunk (BC=16), build b_Akk (strictly lower triangular), then `b_Ai = -b_Akk`, then loop i from 2 to BC: `b_a[i] = -Akk[i,:] (masked <i) + sum_j b_a[j]*b_Ai[j,:]`, updating row i. Then `b_Ai += I`. This computes (I-A0)^{-1}. This is exactly the reference's loop but done per-16-subchunk. Then off-diagonal blocks merged via `b_Ai10 = -Ai11 @ Akk10 @ Ai00` etc. (block triangular inverse). This confirms the algorithm. The `recompute_w_u_fwd` (wy_fast.py) computes w = A @ (exp(g)*k), u = A @ v, qg, kg. Let me read that and the h-pass (chunk_gated_delta_rule_fwd_h) and the o-pass (chunk_gla_fwd_o_gk). These are the other key kernels. But I think I have enough understanding now. Plan for v1 (fused, per (b,h)): ```python @triton.jit def kda_fwd_kernel(q_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, g_ptr, beta_ptr, o_ptr, scale, T, H, K: constexpr, V: constexpr, BT: constexpr, NT: constexpr, BK: constexpr, BV: constexpr, ...): i_bh = program_id(0) i_b = i_bh // H; i_h = i_bh % H # pointers to q,k,v,g,beta,o for this (b,h), strided over T # S = zeros(K, V) in SRAM S = tl.zeros([K, V], dtype=fp32) for n in range(NT): # load q,k,v,g,beta for chunk n: each (BT, K) etc. q = load(...) # (BT, K) k = load(...) v = load(...) # (BT, V) g = load(...) # (BT, K) raw, then cumsum beta = load(...) # (BT,) # cumsum g along BT g = cumsum(g, axis=0) q = q * scale # build A0 (BT, BT) strictly lower tri # A0[i,c] = -beta[i]*sum_d k[c,d]*exp(g[c,d]-g[i,d])*k[i,d] # via kc=k*exp(g), ki=k*exp(-g): A0 = -diag(beta) @ (kc @ ki^T)^T ... # Actually compute G = kc @ ki.T -> G[c,i] = sum_d kc[c,d] ki[i,d] # A0[i,c] = -beta[i]*G[c,i] for c<i ... # forward substitution: Ainv = (I - A0)^{-1} ... # A_final = Ainv * beta[c] (col scale) # w = A_final @ (exp(g)*k) (BT, K) # u = A_final @ v (BT, V) # Aqk[j,c] = sum_d q[c,d]*exp(g[c,d]-g[j,d])*k[j,d], c<=j (BT,BT) lower-tri-incl-diag # qg = q*exp(g) (BT,K) # kg = k*exp(g_last - g) (BT,K) # gd = exp(g_last) (K,) # recurrence: # v_i = u - w @ S # o = qg @ S + Aqk @ v_i # S = S * gd + kg.T @ v_i # store o (BT, V) store(o_ptr..., o) ``` The tricky parts in Triton: 1. cumsum along BT=64. Triton has `tl.cumsum`. Good. 2. Building A0 via kc@ki^T GEMM (BT×K @ K×BT → BT×BT). tl.dot. 3. Forward substitution (I-A0)^{-1}: sequential over BT. This is the hard part in Triton — a loop of 64 iterations, each updating a row. Triton can do this with a python `for` loop (unrolled or not). Each iteration: load row, mask, multiply-accumulate. Might be slow but correct. 4. The various GEMMs: w=A@(exp(g)*k), u=A@v, qg@S, Aqk@v, kg^T@v, w@S. All tl.dot. Let me reconsider the forward substitution. The reference computes M = (I-A0)^{-1} - I via the loop: ``` M = A0 (copy, strictly lower tri, with the -beta scaling and negation already done = A0) for i in 1..BT: M[i,:i] += sum_j M[i,j] * M_before_update[j,:i] # uses A0 for row i and M for rows j<i ``` Wait, I showed M = sum_{p>=1} A0^p where A0 is the strictly-lower-tri (already negated & beta-scaled). (I-A0)^{-1} where (I-A0) is lower-tri with unit diagonal. Forward substitution to solve (I-A0) X = I → X = (I-A0)^{-1}. Forward substitution for lower-tri L (unit diag) solving L X = I: column j of X: X[j,j]=1, and X[i,j] for i>j: X[i,j] = -sum_{k=j}^{i-1} L[i,k] X[k,j] (since L[i,i]=1). Actually, the FLA approach (forward substitution per BC=16 subchunk then block-merge) is the efficient way. Let me adopt that: split BT=64 into 4 subchunks of BC=16. For each 16×16 diagonal block, do the sequential forward-subst (16 iterations). Then merge off-diagonal blocks via matmul (the block-triangular-inverse formula). This parallelizes the sequential part (4 independent 16-step sequences vs 1 64-step) and uses tensor cores for the merges. This is the FLA `chunk_kda_fwd_kernel_inter_solve_fused` structure. +---
+name: kda-algorithm-decomposition
+description: The exact math of the KDA chunk forward (matching reference.py oracle) and the kernel decomposition plan
+metadata:
+  type: project
+---
+
+Problem 02_kda_cutlass: implement chunk-parallel KDA forward on B200 (SM100). Oracle = reference.py. Must NOT import fla.ops.kda etc. FLA repo cloned at /workspace/flash-linear-attention for study only.
+
+**Exact math (must match reference.py, NOT fla's exp2/RCP_LN2 convention):**
+Inputs q,k (B,T,H,K) bf16; v (B,T,H,V) bf16; g (B,T,H,K) fp32; beta (B,T,H) bf16; scale=K^-0.5; chunk_size=64. T%64==0.
+1. q *= scale. Rearrange to (B,H,NT,BT=64,...). **g = cumsum within chunk over the BT axis (reference does g.cumsum(-2) — input g is RAW, must cumsum).**
+2. Intra per chunk: A0[i,c] = -beta[i]*sum_d k[c,d]*exp(g[c,d]-g[i,d])*k[i,d] for c<i (strictly lower tri). Reformulate via kc=k*exp(g), ki=k*exp(-g): G=kc@ki^T (G[c,i]=sum_d kc[c,d]ki[i,d]), A0[i,c]=-beta[i]*G[c,i].
+3. Ainv=(I-A0)^{-1} (= I+A0+A0^2+...). Reference computes via sequential row loop; FLA via BC=16 block forward-subst + block-merge (4 blocks for BT=64). A_final=Ainv*diag(beta_col) but FLA folds beta into the vector instead: w=Ainv@(beta*exp(g)*k), u=Ainv@(beta*v).
+4. Aqk[j,c]=sum_d q[c,d]*exp(g[c,d]-g[j,d])*k[j,d] for c<=j (lower-tri INCL diag), q already scaled. (= intra causal attn; uses kc-style: (q*exp(g))@k^T masked lower-incl-diag... actually q*exp(g[c]) * k[j] needs exp(g[c]-g[j]); use kc_q=q*exp(g), ki=k*exp(-g): Aqk[j,c]=sum_d kc_q[c,d]*ki[j,d], keep c<=j.)
+5. qg=q*exp(g); kg=k*exp(g_last-g) where g_last=g[BT-1] (cumsum at chunk end).
+6. **Inter-chunk recurrence** (S=state K×V, starts 0), per chunk: v_new=u-w@S; o=qg@S_prev+Aqk@v_new; S=S*exp(g_last)+kg^T@v_new.
+
+**Kernel decomposition plan (2 kernels):**
+- K1 intra: parallel over B*H*NT chunks. Outputs w,u (BT×K/×V), qg,kg (BT×K), Aqk (BT×BT). Writes to HBM.
+- K2 fused-recurrence: parallel over B*H * NV V-tiles. Reads w,u,qg,kg,Aqk,g; loops NT chunks sequentially with S(K×BV) in regs; writes o. Fuses h-pass+o-pass (no h/v_new materialized).
+
+**Score:** peak_fraction = geomean over 4 shapes of achieved_tflops/2250 (bf16 peak). regime=compute. RESULT OK if geomean>=0.1. BW floor (single-touch) ~0.30 ceiling for shape1; intermediate traffic lowers it → fuse aggressively. Shapes: (2,1024,8,128), (2,2048,8,128), (1,4096,8,128), (1,2048,4,128). B*H small (4-16) → parallelism is the challenge.
+
+Use `uv run python ...` for everything. Triton needs @jit fns in real files (heredoc breaks). check.py iterates all shapes/seeds/stress(small_qkv atol5e-4, large_qkv atol5e-2)+nominal(atol5e-2). benchmark.py median of 20 iters w/ L2 flush.

+"""Fast dev correctness harness — compares solution vs reference like check.py.
+Usage: uv run python dev_check.py [shape_idx] [--full]
+  default: 1 seed (0), nominal case only, all shapes -> quick.
+  --full: all seeds (42,123,456), all stress cases (like check.py).
+"""
+import sys, argparse
+from pathlib import Path
+import torch
+import reference, shapes, solution
+
+DEVICE = torch.device("cuda:0")
+
+def apply_shape(shape):
+    for k, v in shape.items():
+        setattr(reference, k, v)
+        setattr(solution, k, v)  # keep solution shims in sync too
+
+def make_inputs(seed):
+    torch.manual_seed(seed); torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(seed)
+    return [t.to(DEVICE) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
+
+def maxerr(a, b):
+    a = a.float(); b = b.float()
+    d = (a - b).abs()
+    rel = d / (b.abs() + 1e-6)
+    return d.max().item(), rel.max().item()
+
+def run(shape_idx, full):
+    shape = shapes.SHAPES[shape_idx]
+    apply_shape(shape)
+    init = reference.get_init_inputs()
+    ref_m = reference.Model(*init).to(DEVICE).eval()
+    sol_m = solution.Model(*init).to(DEVICE).eval()
+    try:
+        sol_m.load_state_dict(ref_m.state_dict(), strict=True)
+    except RuntimeError:
+        pass
+    seeds = (42, 123, 456) if full else (0,)
+    scales = [(1.0, 1.0, 1.0)]
+    if full:
+        scales = [(1.0,1.0,1.0), (1e-2,1e-2,1e-2), (2.0,2.0,2.0)]  # nominal, small_qkv, large_qkv (q,k,v)
+    worst = 0.0
+    for seed in seeds:
+        base = make_inputs(seed)
+        for (sq, sk, sv) in scales:
+            inp = [base[0]*sq, base[1]*sk, base[2]*sv, base[3], base[4]]
+            with torch.no_grad():
+                ro = ref_m(*inp)
+                so = sol_m(*inp)
+            ae, re = maxerr(ro, so)
+            worst = max(worst, ae, re)
+            flag = "  " if max(ae,re) < 5e-2 else "**"
+            print(f"{flag}shape{shape_idx} {shape} seed{seed} s({sq},{sk},{sv}): abs={ae:.3e} rel={re:.3e}")
+    return worst
+
+def main():
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("shape", type=int, nargs="?", default=-1)
+    ap.add_argument("--full", action="store_true")
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+    idxs = [0,1,2,3] if args.shape < 0 else [args.shape]
+    overall = 0.0
+    for i in idxs:
+        overall = max(overall, run(i, args.full))
+    tol = 5e-2
+    print(f"\nWORST abs/rel = {overall:.3e}  -> {'PASS' if overall < tol else 'FAIL'} (tol {tol})")
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()

The true (I-A0)^{-1} block (1,0): For a 2×2 block lower-tri system B=[[B00,0],[B10,B11]] (B=I-A0, B00=I-A0_00, B11=I-A0_11, B10=-A0_10), B^{-1}=[[B00^{-1},0],[-B11^{-1} B10 B00^{-1}, B11^{-1}]]. So Akk10 = -A0_10. So FLA Ai10 = -Ai11 @ (-A0_10) @ Ai00 = Ai11 @ A0_10 @ Ai00. ✓ matches the true inverse. So the merge formulas are correct with AkkIJ being the positive (= -A0_block) off-diagonal blocks. And I compute AkkIJ via the GEMM (same as diagonal but for off-diagonal block pairs, no strict-lower masking needed since off-diagonal blocks are fully "below diagonal"). Let me just compute G_full = kc @ ki^T [64,64] (G[c,i] = sum_d kc[c,d]ki[i,d]) once, then A0[i,c] = -beta[i]*G[c,i], i.e., the positive beta-scaled matrix P[i,c] = beta[i]*G[c,i] = beta[i]*G^T[i,c]. So P = diag(beta) @ G^T. Then the blocks of P are the Akk blocks (diagonal blocks need strict-lower masking since within-block the upper part is above-diagonal). 16	    torch.int8: {"atol": 0, "rtol": 0},
17	    torch.int32: {"atol": 0, "rtol": 0},
18	    torch.int64: {"atol": 0, "rtol": 0},
19	}

21	
22	def _coerce_float(x):
23	    """Accept int/float/str scientific-notation as float; pass through dicts."""
24	    if isinstance(x, (int, float)):
25	        return float(x)
26	    if isinstance(x, str):
27	        try:
28	            return float(x)
29	        except ValueError:
30	            return x
31	    return x
32

38	      - a single number (or a string parseable as float, e.g. "5e-2") -> used
39	        as both atol and rtol
40	      - a dict {"atol": ..., "rtol": ...} -> used directly, with values coerced

A tf32 GEMM rounds the 8-bit inputs to... well tf32 keeps 10 bits, and the inputs already only have 8 meaningful bits, so tf32 doesn't lose anything! So tf32 GEMM of bf16-origin data ≈ fp32 GEMM of bf16-origin data, to within bf16 precision. But the DECAY products (kc = k*exp(g), ki = k*exp(-g)) — these are computed in fp32 (k bf16 * exp(g) fp32 = fp32 with ~8-bit k precision but the product is fp32). +"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form — custom Triton kernels for B200 (SM100).
+
+Two-kernel design (matches the FLA chunk decomposition, reimplemented from scratch):
+  1. kda_intra_kernel  — parallel over (chunk, b*h). Builds the intra-chunk
+     delta-rule inverse Ainv=(I-A0)^{-1}, the causal intra-attention Aqk, and the
+     per-chunk projections w,u,qg,kg + the chunk-end decay gd.
+  2. kda_recur_kernel  — parallel over (v-tile, b*h). Fused state recurrence +
+     output: sequential over chunks, S(K,BV) in registers, no h/v_new round-trip.
+
+Math mirrors reference.py exactly (natural exp, in-chunk cumsum of g applied here).
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["B200"]
+
+
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# (I - A0)^{-1} for a strictly-lower-triangular nilpotent A0 (BT x BT).
+# Forward substitution: row i of (I-A0)^{-1} = A0[i,:] + sum_j A0[i,j] * inv[j,:].
+# Row i is extracted from the constant A0 via a masked reduction (Triton has no
+# dynamic row indexing of a tile, so we broadcast a one-hot mask and sum).
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+@triton.jit
+def _invert_strict_lower(A0, BT: tl.constexpr):
+    ar = tl.arange(0, BT)
+    b_Ai = A0
+    for i in tl.static_range(1, BT):
+        m_i = (ar == i)
+        row = tl.sum(A0 * m_i[:, None], axis=0)                 # A0[i,:]
+        new_row = row + tl.sum(row[:, None] * b_Ai, axis=0)
+        b_Ai = tl.where(m_i[:, None], new_row, b_Ai)
+    b_Ai = b_Ai + (ar[:, None] == ar[None, :]).to(tl.float32)   # + I
+    return b_Ai
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def kda_intra_kernel(
+    q_ptr, k_ptr, v_ptr, g_ptr, beta_ptr,
+    w_ptr, u_ptr, qg_ptr, kg_ptr, Aqk_ptr, gd_ptr,
+    scale, T, NT,
+    H: tl.constexpr, K: tl.constexpr, V: tl.constexpr,
+    BT: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    i_t = tl.program_id(0)
+    i_bh = tl.program_id(1)
+    i_b = i_bh // H
+    i_h = i_bh % H
+
+    ar = tl.arange(0, BT)
+
+    # base pointers (tensors are (B,T,H,*), contiguous)
+    q_b = q_ptr + i_b * T * H * K + i_h * K
+    k_b = k_ptr + i_b * T * H * K + i_h * K
+    g_b = g_ptr + i_b * T * H * K + i_h * K
+    v_b = v_ptr + i_b * T * H * V + i_h * V
+    beta_b = beta_ptr + i_b * T * H + i_h
+    w_b = w_ptr + i_b * T * H * K + i_h * K
+    u_b = u_ptr + i_b * T * H * V + i_h * V
+    qg_b = qg_ptr + i_b * T * H * K + i_h * K
+    kg_b = kg_ptr + i_b * T * H * K + i_h * K
+    Aqk_b = Aqk_ptr + i_b * T * H * BT + i_h * BT
+    gd_b = gd_ptr + (i_b * NT + i_t) * H * K + i_h * K
+
+    t0 = i_t * BT
+
+    # ---- load chunk: q,k,g [BT,K]; beta [BT]; v [BT,V] ----
+    p_q = tl.make_block_ptr(q_b, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_k = tl.make_block_ptr(k_b, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_g = tl.make_block_ptr(g_b, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_v = tl.make_block_ptr(v_b, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
+    p_beta = tl.make_block_ptr(beta_b, (T,), (H,), (t0,), (BT,), (0,))
+
+    b_q = tl.load(p_q).to(tl.float32)
+    b_k = tl.load(p_k).to(tl.float32)
+    b_g = tl.load(p_g).to(tl.float32)            # raw per-token log-decay
+    b_v = tl.load(p_v).to(tl.float32)
+    b_beta = tl.load(p_beta).to(tl.float32)
+
+    b_q = b_q * scale
+
+    # in-chunk cumsum of g (resets at each chunk because we load one chunk)
+    b_gc = tl.cumsum(b_g, axis=0)
+    g_last = tl.sum(b_g, axis=0)                  # gc[BT-1,:] = total decay over chunk, [K]
+    gd = tl.exp(g_last)                           # exp(g_last), [K]
+
+    exp_g = tl.exp(b_gc)
+    neg_g = tl.exp(-b_gc)
+    kc = b_k * exp_g                              # [BT,K]
+    ki = b_k * neg_g                              # [BT,K]
+    kcq = b_q * exp_g                             # [BT,K]  (= qg)
+
+    # ---- A0: A0[i,c] = -beta[i]*sum_d k[c,d]*exp(g[c,d]-g[i,d])*k[i,d], c<i ----
+    # G[c,i] = sum_d kc[c,d]*ki[i,d]  ->  P[i,c]=beta[i]*G[c,i]=beta[i]*trans(G)[i,c]
+    G = tl.dot(kc, tl.trans(ki))                  # [BT,BT], G[c,i]
+    P = b_beta[:, None] * tl.trans(G)             # [BT,BT], P[i,c] = -A0[i,c]
+    m_strict = ar[:, None] > ar[None, :]
+    A0 = tl.where(m_strict, -P, 0.0)
+    Ainv = _invert_strict_lower(A0, BT)           # (I-A0)^{-1}, [BT,BT]
+
+    # ---- w = Ainv @ (beta*kc), u = Ainv @ (beta*v) ----
+    bkc = b_beta[:, None] * kc
+    bv = b_beta[:, None] * b_v
+    b_w = tl.dot(Ainv, bkc)                       # [BT,K]
+    b_u = tl.dot(Ainv, bv)                        # [BT,V]
+
+    # ---- Aqk[j,c] = sum_d q[c,d]*exp(g[c,d]-g[j,d])*k[j,d], c<=j ----
+    # Gq[c,j] = sum_d kcq[c,d]*ki[j,d]; Aqk[j,c]=Gq[c,j]=trans(Gq)[j,c], keep c<=j
+    Gq = tl.dot(kcq, tl.trans(ki))               # [BT,BT], Gq[c,j]
+    Aqk = tl.where(m_strict | (ar[:, None] == ar[None, :]), tl.trans(Gq), 0.0)
+
+    # ---- kg = k*exp(g_last - g) = k * gd * neg_g ----
+    b_kg = b_k * (gd[None, :] * neg_g)
+
+    # ---- stores ----
+    p_w = tl.make_block_ptr(w_b, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_u = tl.make_block_ptr(u_b, (T, V), (H * V, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, V), (1, 0))
+    p_qg = tl.make_block_ptr(qg_b, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_kg = tl.make_block_ptr(kg_b, (T, K), (H * K, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, K), (1, 0))
+    p_Aqk = tl.make_block_ptr(Aqk_b, (T, BT), (H * BT, 1), (t0, 0), (BT, BT), (1, 0))
+    tl.store(p_w, b_w.to(p_w.dtype.element_ty))
+    tl.store(p_u, b_u.to(p_u.dtype.element_ty))
+    tl.store(p_qg, kcq.to(p_qg.dtype.element_ty))
+    tl.store(p_kg, b_kg.to(p_kg.dtype.element_ty))
+    tl.store(p_Aqk, Aqk.to(p_Aqk.dtype.element_ty))
+    tl.store(gd_b + tl.arange(0, K), gd)
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def kda_recur_kernel(
+    w_ptr, u_ptr, qg_ptr, kg_ptr, Aqk_ptr

... (4408 more chars)

1	"""Kimi Delta Attention (KDA) forward, chunk form — custom Triton kernels for B200 (SM100).
2	
3	Two-kernel design (matches the FLA chunk decomposition, reimplemented from scratch):
4	  1. kda_intra_kernel  — parallel over (chunk, b*h). Builds the intra-chunk
5	     delta-rule inverse Ainv=(I-A0)^{-1}, the causal intra-attention Aqk, and the
6	     per-chunk projections w,u,qg,kg + the chunk-end decay gd.
7	  2. kda_recur_kernel  — parallel over (v-tile, b*h). Fused state recurrence +
8	     output: sequential over chunks, S(K,BV) in registers, no h/v_new round-trip.
9	
10	Math mirrors reference.py exactly (natural exp, in-chunk cumsum of g applied here).
11	"""
12	from __future__ import annotations
13	import torch
14	import triton
15	import triton.language as tl
16	
17	OP_TYPE = "linear_attention"
18	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
19	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["B200"]
20	
21	
22	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
23	# (I - A0)^{-1} for a strictly-lower-triangular nilpotent A0 (BT x BT).
24	# Forward substitution: row i of (I-A0)^{-1} = A0[i,:] + sum_j A0[i,j] * inv[j,:].
25	# Row i is extracted from the constant A0 via a masked reduction (Triton has no
26	# dynamic row indexing of a tile, so we broadcast a one-hot mask and sum).
27	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
28	@triton.jit
29	def _invert_strict_lower(A0, BT: tl.constexpr):
30	    ar = tl.arange(0, BT)

28	@triton.jit
29	def _invert_strict_lower(A0, BT: tl.constexpr):
30	    ar = tl.arange(0, BT)
31	    b_Ai = A0
32	    for i in tl.static_range(1, BT):
33	        m_i = (ar == i)
34	        row = tl.sum(A0 * m_i[:, None], axis=0)                 # A0[i,:]
